4b:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["But a double-stringified value like ",["$","code",null,{"className":"nextra-code","dir":"ltr","children":"\"{\\\\\"type\\\\\":\\\\\"card\\\\\"}\""}]," passes through unscathed — it’s already valid JSON (it’s a string). 4c:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["Typia’s ",["$","code",null,{"className":"nextra-code","dir":"ltr","children":"parse()"}]," works differently. It parses greedily while ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"consulting the schema"}],". When it encounters a string where the schema expects an object, it re-enters ",["$","code",null,{"className":"nextra-code","dir":"ltr","children":"parse()"}]," on that string, applying the same lenient recovery. c0:["$","p",null,{"className":"x:not-first:mt-[1.25em] x:leading-7","children":["With native TypeScript types, recursive references are name lookups — ",["$","strong",null,{"children":"O(N) linear"}],".
